Acknowledgements
While working in Kathmandu for the Nepal-German Manuscript Preservation Project
(NGMPP) Dr. Franz-Karl Ehrhard microfilmed a manuscript entitled Mdo snags bka'
'gyur dkar chag, i.e. the register (of the) Kanjur (which comprises) Sutra and Tantra ",
which indicates that it is a full-fledged catalogue of a Tibetan Kanjur. Through the kind
services of Tulku Tsewang, Nampakünden (Jumla area ), it was procured from Mu gu
district (West Nepal) during the Nampakünden expedition (November 20 to December
3, 1988). A copy of it was kindly sent to me. I take pleasure in extending my sincerest
thanks not only to Dr. F.- K . Ehrhard, but also to Prof. Dr. Albrecht Wezler, Hamburg,
for his kind help in obtaining permission to use this text and to Sani Maiya Rana, Acting
Chief Research Officer, National Archives, Kathmandu, for granting that permission.
No other manuscript or blockprinted edition entitled Mdo snags bka' 'gyur dkar chag
has been found so far in spite of the endeavours of Dr. F.-K . Ehrhard, Dr. Christoph
Cüppers and Dr. Klaus-Dieter Mathes, for which I would like to offer them my best
thanks.
More than a dozen years ago in the writings of Nor chen Kun dga ' bzan po (A .D .
1382-1456) I happened upon a brief catalogue of a canonical collection entitled Bka' 'gyur
ro cog gi dkar chag bstan pa gsal ba 'i sgron me, i.e. " The Catalogue of the Kanjur,
[named ) the Lamp (for) Elucidating the Doctrine" . At first glance it seems to comprise
a full catalogue of a Kanjur; as a matter of fact, however, it describes the Tantra section
only, as I found out when first reading it. The whole of Nor chen 's (Bka ' 'gyur ro cog
gi dkar chag) Bstan pa gsal ba 'i sgron me turned out to be contained in the Mdo snags
bka' 'gyur dkar chag which does not only cover the rgyud section, but comprises the
'dul ba, the ses phyin and the mdo sections as well. I tender my thanks to Prof. Dr. David
Jackson for his kind help in searching for a manuscript or another edition of the Bstan
pa gsal ba ' sgron me, which could not be traced, though.
The study of this Kanjur catalogue was first announced in a brief paper entitled " Pre
liminary Notes on Nor chen's Kanjur Catalogue" which I was permitted to present to
the 6 Seminar of the International Association for Tibetan Studies, held at Fager
nes/Norway.' A former, i.e. 1994 version of the following edition did not yet contain
references to earlier Sa skya pa dkar chags which have now been added on the basis of
Cf. EIMER 1994; the following "Introductory Notes" rely on material utilized for this paper

Introductory Notes
The sources used
The Mdo snags bka ' 'gyur dkar chag is written in fair du med script, the volume head
ings and a few - mainly secondary - syllables are given in dbu can. At the left-hand
side the leaves bear double foliation running from 1 to 34 and from 106 to 139. Added
to these is the siglum ne, representing in ordinary calculation the number 94 , which indi
cates that this text, together with the ensuing Bstan 'gyur snags phyogs dkar chag, formed
part of a larger set of fascicles or volumes. It cannot be settled at present whether or not
the marginal siglum and the foliation refer to a Kanjur edition or to a collection of the
bka ''bum of Nor chen Kun dga' bzan po or of the Great Sa skya pa Teachers. That this
collection was most probably not the Kanjur described may be seen from the number
of volumes listed: there are 30 volumes of the Tantrayana and 108 of the Päramitāyāna.
In the Sa skya pa 'i bka ' 'bum , the Complete Works of the five Great Sa skya pa
Masters printed in Derge in A .D . 1736 , the Bka' 'gyur ro cog gi dkar chag bstan pa
gsal ba'i sgron me covers 11 leaves in all. The leaves carry a double foliation as well;
the lettera appears as marginal siglum , here denoting - in spite of its numerical value
30 - the final volume of Nor chen's bka' 'bum . From the intermediate chapter colophons
we deduce a somewhat more elaborate title, viz . Bde bar gśegs pa'i gsun rab 'gyur ro
cog gi dkar chag bstan pa gsal ba'i sgron me. The following two pages of the Sa skya

cm .

original foliations and put in parentheses.

contain a text entitled Bstan 'gyur dkar chag" comprising the brief titles
of those groups of texts which are essential for a complete Tanjur. With the ensuing Rdo
rje theg pa'i bstan bcos 'gyur ro tshal gyi dkar chag" we have a detailed catalogue for
the Tantra section of the Tanjur prepared at Glo bo Brag dkar gyi gtsug lag khan." The
same dkar chag appears under the title Bstan 'gyur shags phyogs dkar chag in the manuscript
filmed by the NGMPP, its initial title Rdo rje theg pa'i bstan bcos 'gyur ro ' shal gyi dkar
chag gsan snags bstan pa rgyas byed indicates that Tantra texts only are listed therein."
Concept of this publication
The present paper gives a " Structured Edition" of the dkar chag to the Early Mustang
Kanjur, i.e. the Mdo snags bka ' 'gyur dkar chag, together with the Bstan pa gsal ba 'i
sgron me. This edition counts the individual texts listed in the catalogue" and prints the
titles's registered therein in separate paragraphs. The text common to both text witnesses
is reproduced in the form it has in the blockprinted edition . Variant readings occurring
in the manuscript are noted in brackets or in footnotes. The xylograph seems to be more
carefully edited than the manuscript; both versions obviously go back to the same
exemplar. The second main part relies on the Mdo snags bka ' 'gyur dkar chag only,
as this is the sole version accessible.

nams rgya mtsho 1969:
349/2/6 -349/4 /6 .
" It covers foll. 6261-78a3 (270b1-286a3) only, reprinted in Bsod nams rgya mtsho 1969:

12 This is the name found in the brief colophon. Brag dkar is one of the three great monas
teries of Mustang, cf. JACKSON 1984: 43, note 6. The monastery Brag dkar theg chen glin was
founded during Nor chen 's first visit to Lo, cf. op. cit.: 154, note 20. This monastery is located
within the walls of Lo Man than (Glo smon than ).

ber given in the Sa skya pa 'i bka ' 'bum edition (fol. 76a2 and 284a2 respectively). In the manu

chad became erased.

Introductory Notes
References to other catalogues are added in smaller type with the aim of enabling
the reader to find parallel texts. A great number of titles listed are provided with cross
references to Bu ston's plan of a complete Tibetan Buddhist canon comprised in his Chos
'byur " as well as to the Derge, Tog (Stog) Palace, Peking, Narthang, and Phug brag
Kanjurs. In the Tantra section references to the early Tantra catalogues by Grags pa rgyal
mtshan (A .D . 1147-1216), 'Phags pa Blo gros rgyal mtshan ( A .D . 1235-1280),18 and
Bu ston Rin chen grub ( A .D . 1290 -1364)" are included .
Together with several cross references divergent versions of the titles are given ,
because in the catalogues the titles often appear in a shortened or not always standardized
form . It is difficult to identify the texts on the basis of identical or similar titles only.
In case the Mustang catalogue lists the same title twice or similar ones, no reference to
other collections appears at the second place. Wherever the Mustang Kanjur catalogue
adds to the bare title a note referring to the size or to the translators of the text in question
the identification becomes easier, provided that corresponding information can be culled
from dkar chags or catalogues consulted for comparison. As keys to the material
presented concordances and indices are added . There is an index of titles and another
of personal names; in the latter a cross reference system covering the different parts of
a complete name is introduced.
Origin and structure of the Early Mustang catalogue
In the Early Mustang Kanjur catalogue the prose part of the introductory passage common
to both versions reports that the " ruler A ma dpal bzan po rgyal mtshan, born in the upper
part of the country Glo bo of Mna' ris", ordered a new Kanjur to be prepared, because
in his realm " in consequence of the very long time elapsed several volumes had decayed
and at that juncture no complete volume of the Kanjur existed in any one place " 24 This

the footnotes.

points to the “Golden Kanjur " having been prepared for the royal family of Mustang.
Following a Tibetan informant, MICHEL PEISSEL refers in this connection to the biography
of Kun dga' bzan po , which reports that in A .D . 1436 it was decided to produce a new
Kanjur in Mustang, that it was finished only eleven years later, i.e. in A.D . 1447, and
that a catalogue comprising the individual titles of all the texts was composed.26
The final portion of the introduction 
sketches the intended plan of the ensuing text. The
following two main sections are announced there:
(A .) the cycle of texts belonging to the Vajrayana and
(B .) that belonging to the Päramitāyana ."
The Bstan pa gsal ba'i sgron me registers only the texts pertaining to the Vajrayāna (A .).
This part of the catalogue consists of three chapters (skabs) which list the contents of
twenty -one volumes rgyud 'bum , of three volumes gzuns 'dus and of six volumes gzuns
'bum , 30 volumes in all. The number of texts contained in each volume is noted at the
end of its short description. Differences between these numbers and the actual number
of titles given in some volumes will be noted at the corresponding place of the " Structured
Edition" given below . It is noteworthy that mainly in the rgyud 'bum section some further
information as to the size of the text in question or to its translators appears along with
the titles; this is generally not the case in the later parts of the Mustang Kanjur catalogue.
In addition to the Vajrayāna or Tantra section the Mdo snags bka ' 'gyur dkar chag
also covers the second main section (B.) which is formed by paragraphs of different length .
The texts of the Vinaya section are registered first starting [23a1]), followed by the Pra
jnaparamita texts (starting [2362]). At the start of the Sutra section ([24a2]) two subsections
are named , the former is classified as mdo sil bu pa or mdo mans - this stands for the
Sutras of smaller or limited size - the latter as mdo che bži (starting [31a7]), i.e. the

Introductory Notes
sections is that the latter does not note the number of texts contained in a volume at its
end , which is simply indicated by mams bzugs, mams bzugs so or the like. Therefore
one cannot help suspecting that the catalogue of the Vinaya, Prajāpäramitã and Sätra
texts was compiled by an author other than Nor chen Kun dga' bzan po.
Five stanzas structure the Vajrayāna part of the catalogue. After listing text 083 the follow
ing verse appears (54a6 -b1) [9b7-10a1]:
thabs ses zun jug I'jug] ston pa mchog gi rgyud [brgyud]
mtha' drug tshul bis [bzi'i) gsan bas [ba] rgyas btab pa
zab mo'i (mo) rnal 'byor bla na med pa'i mdo
bcu phrag bdun dan bdun gyis lhag pa (pas) bzugs
In its first two lines this quatrain gives the number of titles belonging to the highest Tantra
subcategory thabs ses rab zuń 'jug gi rgyud - which otherwise is called gnis su med
pa 'i rgyud - , viz . six. A subdivision of the uppermost Tantra class is already attested
in the Kyai rdo rje'i rgyud 'bum gyi dkar chag by Grags pa rgyal mtshan who presents
a concise subdivision of the Mahayoga (i.e. the Anuttarayogatantra) texts under three
headings. For this organization the key terms used are the following: thabs (upaya), ses
rab (prajna), and gñis su med pa (advaya). This system appears in a slightly altered and
more developed form in the catalogues to all the Kanjurs which belong to the Tshal pa
and Them spans ma lines of canonical transmission . There the three terms are given
in inverted order, with only ses rab remaining in the middle position and the second and
third categories being further subdivided. According to Bu ston Rin chen grub the initial
portion of the fully developed structure is as follows:
rnal 'byor bla na med pa 'i rgyud (Anuttarayogatantra)
1. gnis su med pa'i rgyud (advaya )
2. Ses rab rnal 'byor ma'i rgyud (prajñā°)
2.1 rigs drug mnam par ston pa'i rgyud

Introductory Notes
The last two lines of the first stanza mention seventy -seven as the number of titles within
the rnal 'byor bla na med pa'i rgyud category, which we may understand as "the remain
ing) titles belonging to the Anuttarayogatantra" . Thereby we learn that the compiler re
gards the first eighty-three texts listed as forming the uppermost class of the Tantras.
At the beginning of the rgyud 'bum section the six texts pertaining to the Hevajratantra
are given which the first stanza classifies as belonging to the gris su med pa 'i rgyud
category. This accords with the catalogue prepared by 'Phags pa Blo gros rgyal mtshan ,
whereas Grags pa rgyal mtshan considers the Advayatantra to be the third subdivision
of the Anuttarayogatantra. From the time of Bu ston Rin chen grub the Hevajra cycle
was regarded as a ses rab kyi rgyudas. With the Samputatantra this first cycle of seven
texts ends, it is marked by a brief intermediate colophon." The texts thereafter up to 037
belong to the Samvaratantra cycle, with 019 the ra lili skor starts, which is styled as the
bšad rgyud of Samvara. In the common Kanjurs this cycle comprises more than double
the number of texts. For the cycle of Kalacakra eight texts are registered as appearing
in the beginning of volume ja (7) of the rgyud 'bum section; the texts in question are
counted as 055-062.99

The third quatrain occurs after text 120 at the end of the first chapter (skabs dan po).
it reads as follows (563) [13a3-4):
tin 'dzin mtshan ma med pa'i mal "byor dan
lus nag mam (yid) par (gsum ) dag (enam ) par byed (dag] pa'i tsbul
gñis med sbyor ba bya dan spyod pa'i mdo
bcu phrag gñis dan dgu yis brgyan pa bzugs
This verse counts twenty -nine texts of the fourth and third Tantra categories, viz. of the
bya ba'i rgyud (Kriyatantra) and of the spyod pa'i rgyud (Caryätantra)" . The number
of titles listed , viz. twenty-three," and that of texts given in the third quatrain which is
found at the end of the skabs dan po do not agree. In this way the stanzas quoted so far
indicate the basic pattern according to which the first chapter of the Mustang Kanjur,
the rgyud 'bum , is organized . The general scheme for the Tantra sections of the common
Kanjurs is as under:
(a) the rnal 'byor bla na med pa'i rgyud (Anuttarayogatantra)
(b) the rnal 'byor gyi rgyud (Yogatantra ),
(c) the spyod pa'i rgyud (Caryätantra), and
(d) the bya ba 'i rgyud (Kriyatantra).
It is remarkable that both the quatrain and the catalogue give the two lower Tantra
categories not in descending, but in ascending order. Within the skabs dan po, viz. the
rgyud 'bum , we find brief remarks announcing the start of a new Tantra category at the
following places: one directly after the first stanza" at the commencement of the second
Tantra class, the Yogatantra, and another after the second stanza at the beginning of
the fourth class, the spyod pa'i rgyud (Caryātantra), which is followed by the third one,
the bya ba'i rgyud (Kriyātantra)."

This second dharani collection comprises 190 texts in all, but the stanza mentions as many

the whole of the Vajrayana section only 491 texts are listed . This difference is in need
of explanation . We may assume that after the catalogue was completed by 
Nor chen some
more texts were added , or that Nor chen relied upon an earlier dkar chag, the structure
of which was taken over in spite of the additions. Therefore, the questions

Introductory Notes
is regarded here as forming the second main part of the description of an Early Mustang
Kanjur, there is some probability that Kun dga' bzan po was not its direct compiler. The
Early Mustang Kanjur catalogue is less structured than the canonical collection listed by
Grags pa rgyal mtshan more than 200 years earlier and far less so than the common
Kanjurs. This may be due to the situation of the literary tradition of the Buddhist scriptures
in Mustang in the time of king A ma dpal bzan po rgyal mtshan, when several volumes
of the Kanjur were destroyed and no complete volume was accessible at one place. It
would be quite possible that Nor chen, holding the holy tradition of Mustang in high
esteem , collected the scattered texts there and arranged the Tantras following a loose
scheme only.
The value of the Early Mustang catalogue
As long as no copy of the Early Mustang Kanjur becomes accessible, the main value of
the catalogue published here lies in the information culled from the arrangement of the
individual texts and from the names of translators given together with some of the titles.
The structure of the catalogue to the Early Mustang Kanjur is a specific feature not
to be met with in the common Kanjurs: to the general Tantra section a gzu 's 'dus of three
volumes and a gzuns 'bum of six volumes are added . In the Kanjurs belonging to the
Tshal pa branch of transmission we find a two-volume gzunis 'dus as well," which
originally was a separate collection . Therefore we may assume that in the case of our
catalogue two such additional dharani collections are included.
By a lucky chance a trace of one of these additional collections has shown up, unless
we assume that the fragment in question belonged to a volume of the Early Mustang
Kanjur.” The three leaves foliated in the margin as 472 to 474 contain the final portion
and the brief colophon of
(1) the 'Phags pa dkyil 'khor brgyad pa zes bya ba theg pa chen po'i mdo.
This is followed by
(2) the 'Phags pa 'od (8)zer can ges bya ba'i gzuhs
and by the beginning of
(3) the 'Phags pa gžan 'brum rab tu ti bar byed pa'i mdo.

Introductory Notes
These three brief Dhäranis are recorded one after another as the 24h to 26 out of 13154
texts in the second volume (kha) of the gzuńs 'dus section.
In the second main part of the Early Mustang Kanjur catalogue the group of the mdo
che bzi, the " Four Great Sütras", appears as final section, which covers the myan 'das
chen, i.e. the most extensive Mahāparinirvānasūtra, the phal po che, i.e. the Avatamsaka,
the dkon mchog brtsegs pa , i.e . the Ratnakūta, a second myan 'das chen which seems
to have been added erroneously, and the dam pa'i chos dran pa, i.e. the Saddharma
smrtyupasthāna.
In the common Kanjurs the sections phal chen and dkon brtsegs follow the Prajña
päramitā texts, whereas the Mahāparinirvāņa section, if it is present at all, is placed after
the general Sutra section. A separate division for the Saddharmasmrtyupasthäna is not
known from the common Kanjurs. The order of the " Four Great Sütras" appears in the
"Golden Kanjur of Tsarang" too in the form of the subsections myan 'das, phal chen,
dkon brtsegs, and dran pa ñer búag .
Especially in the rgyud 'bum chapter (skabs dan po) some pandi tas and lo tstsha bas
are mentioned whose names we do not find transmitted together with the corresponding
titles in the common Kanjurs.
For the Nes (or: Mnon) par brjod pa 'i rgyud bla ma, e.g ., the following translator's
names are given : Mkhan po Jnanasri, Blo gros sñin po and Dge slon Rab zi." Otherwise
we have Dipamkaraśrijñāna and Rin chen bzan po as translators of this text and Jnanasri
and Khyun po Chos kyi brtson 'grus as revisers. * The Phug brag Kanjur dkar chag in
turn gives divergent names, viz . as translators Pandit Jñänākara and Lo tstsha ba Rigs
pa gzon nu and as revisers Pandit Prabhākara and Dge slon Säkya ye ses. The only name

common to these three traditions is Jnanaśri or Jänakara , but he appears sometimes as
translator, sometimes as reviser. As the other persons named are different, the actual
wording of this text may disagree in the three traditions referred to .
Another example of this kind is the 'Jam dpal rtsa ba'i rtog pa which according to
the Early Mustang Kanjur catalogue was translated by Dpal Dga' ba'i bốes gñen and Lo
tstsha ba Man 'or Chos kyi ses rab, whereas the other sources name Pandit Kumarakalaša
and Säkya blo gros." Therefore , it could well be that the Early Mustang Kanjur had as
its basis , at least for the texts named , manuscript material differing from that used in the
other 
commonly known traditions of the Kanjur.
The Mustang Kanjur comprises nine out of the twelve chapters of the Vamnärhavarnastotra
by Mätrceta (430 , (3) to (11 )), whereas the Western Tibetan Phug brag Kanjur covers
at one place ten chapters and at another all the twelve chapters of that text. This seems
to point to a literary tradition of the Buddhist scriptures in westernmost Tibet which has
remained uninfluenced by other sources since early times . The prose introduction to the
Early Mustang Kanjur catalogue seems to refer to this separate tradition by saying that
" especially in the country of Mra' ris the jewel of the Teaching which started from the
time of the later propagation of the Teaching remained unbarmed for a long time" .

Indices
Tibetan Titles
This Index contains the titles found in the Mdo snags bka ' 'gyur dkar chag and the Bka '
'gyur ro cog gi dkar chag bstan pa gsal ba'i sgron me edited above in the " Structured
Edition ". Divergent titles from other dkar chags and catalogues used for the purpose of
comparison in the body of the "Structured Edition" are also included .
Each entry in this Index ends with the reference to the bold printed ) text number
given in the " Structured Edition ". If it is preceded by the reference to another catalogue
the entry lists the title as given therein, a pointer (- ) between the two references in
dicates that one and the same item is referred to. A simple gap between two text
numbers indicates that titles are identical.
For reducing the number of entries to a reasonable rate titles with identical initial
syllables referring to the same entry in the " Structured Edition " are combined into one
lemma; divergent titles within a single entry are separated by semicolons. By means of
typographic devices it is possible to read the divergent forms of a title: the identical
syllables are italicised, the different portion from the parallel source is added in smaller
type, the last common syllable is repeated in italics after the bold printed reference
number and a small circle [° ] the Indian Devanagari sign for abbreviation - is put
above the line.
Minor variants occurring in the titles are noted in parentheses, the enclosed syllable (8)
substitute the last preceding syllable(s), the source is indicated after the variant reading
by the siglum only. In some cases where at the beginning of an entry the title of a
superior text is referred to - e.g. by a deictic pronoun (like de') - the explanation
appears in parentheses, too, but without reference to any source.
